id="MJXp-Span-78" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-79">N</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-80">a</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-81" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-82">x</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-83"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-84">T</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-85">i</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-86">C</span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-3"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">T</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>x</mi><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup><mo>+</mo><mi>x</mi><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="italic">e</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">→</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>x</mi></mrow></msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">T</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(3)</span></div></div><p></p><p>Charge (Na<sup>+</sup> extraction from TiC nanoflowers):</p><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq4"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-87"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-88"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-89"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-90"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-91"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-92" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-93">N</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-94">a</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-95" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-96">x</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-97"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-98">T</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-99">i</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-100">C</span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-101"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-102" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">→</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-103"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-104"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-105">T</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-106">i</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-107">C</span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-108" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-109">x</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-110"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-111" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-112">N</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-113">a</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-114" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-115">+</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-116" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-117">x</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-118"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-119" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-120">e</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-121" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-122">−</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-4"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>x</mi></mrow></msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">T</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">→</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">T</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>x</mi><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup><mo>+</mo><mi>x</mi><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="italic">e</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(4)</span></div></div><p></p><p>The unique nanoflower morphology of TiC enhances electronic transport and sodium diffusion thanks to its high surface area and porosity. This structure ensures rapid electron mobility and swift sodium-ion diffusion, minimizing local current density and preventing performance degradation (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>e). These properties contribute to a homogeneous ionic flux, maintaining electrode integrity and prolonging the cycle life. Overall, the TiC nanoflower anode’s characteristics significantly boost the performance and efficiency of SIBs.</p><p>A full cell configuration was constructed by utilizing TiC nanoflowers as the anode material and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO4)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) as the cathode material (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>a). NVP holds great potential as a cathode material for fast-charging and long-cycling SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref59" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref59" aria-label="reference 59">(59)</a> <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 5</a>b and <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c show the rate performance of the Na-ion full cell at current densities of 0.1, 0.25, and 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. When the current density increased from 0.1 to 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, approximately 57.9% of the capacity was retained. The galvanostatic charge–discharge curve (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03597/suppl_file/nl4c03597_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S16</a>) at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> between 0.01 and 3.0 V shows a high discharge capacity of 53.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> based on the anode mass. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>d illustrates the cycling performance tested at a current density of 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Notably, the full cell maintained a discharge capacity of 53.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 20 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>e provides a schematic illustration of the TiC//NVP full cell in practical application, successfully demonstrating its capability by illuminating an LED indicator (working voltage and current: 2.1 V, 10 mA). These results suggest that TiC nanoflowers have a high potential for practical applications in SIBs. To further optimize the performance of sodium-ion full cells, pairing the TiC nanoflower anode with various cathode materials and selecting suitable electrolytes can be explored.</p><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03597/asset/images/medium/nl4c03597_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03597/asset/images/large/nl4c03597_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. Sodium-ion full cells. (a) Schematic diagram of an assembled TiC nanoflowers//NVP full cell. (b) Rate performance of a TiC nanoflowers//NVP full cell at different current rates. (c) The charging–discharging platform of a TiC nanoflowers//NVP full cell. (d) Cycling performance of a TiC nanoflowers//NVP full cell at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (e) Image of lighted LED powered by a coin-type TiC nanoflowers//NVP full cell.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03597/asset/images/large/nl4c03597_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="last">In summary, we successfully synthesized TiC nanoflowers with a porous structure using a simple and controllable CVD method. The thickness and yield of nanoflowers increased with extended growth time from 30 to 120 min and rising temperatures from 850 to 1050 °C. These TiC nanoflower-based SIBs demonstrated a high reversible specific capacity of 73.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 2500 cycles, with a capacity retention rate of 80.81%. Additionally, the full sodium-ion cell utilizing TiC nanoflowers as the anode and NVP as the cathode exhibited a large reversible capacity and excellent cycling stability. While hard carbon and alloy materials are leading Na-ion battery anodes, our study introduces TiC nanoflowers with a unique porous structure, high conductivity, and chemical stability. This morphology enhances Na<sup>+</sup> storage, electron transport, and cycling stability, offering a prolonged cycle life. Additionally, TiC nanoflowers can serve as conductive scaffolds for other energy storage materials like sulfur and silicon. The nanoflowers reported in this work provide alternative anodes for SIBs, combining high capacity, stability, and efficiency, ideal for advanced energy storage systems.</p><div class="NLM_back"><div                         cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Design of Unique MoSe2-Carbon Nanobowl Particles Endows Superior Alkali Metal-Ion Storage Beyond Lithium</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Lai; Li, Jie; Wang, Gongrui; Peng, Bo; Liu, Rong; Shi, Liang; Zhang, Genqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">61116-61128</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Attracted by the rich earth abundance and low-cost advantages, alkali metal-ion (Na/K)-based energy storage devices have attracted wide interest as promising candidates for energy economizing in recent years.  Unfortunately, the lack of suitable host materials with high capacity and long life span for alkali metal-ion storage has severely impeded their practical application in large-scale energy storage devices.  Herein, we present a promising anode candidate composed of ultrasmall MoSe2 clusters embedded in a nitrogen-doped hollow carbon nanobowl substrate to form unique MoSe2-Carbon nanobowl particles (denoted as MoSe2(CNB)).  MoSe2(CNB) demonstrates exceptional electrochem. properties for alkali metal-ion storage including sodium and potassium.  In situ Raman spectroscopy and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. measurements reveal the possible reason for the high performance of MoSe2(CNB).  Notably, the assembled potassium-ion hybrid capacitors could manifest an extraordinary energy d. of 130.7 W h kg-1 at 0.2 A g-1, a high power d. of 13,607 W kg-1, and an enviable cycle life after 6000 cycles, further reflecting the great developmental potential for energy storage devices in practical applications.  This work provides a new method to design functional nanostructures for electrode materials to drive the development and application of possible energy storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref3" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202000473"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineering of polyanion type cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries: toward higher energy/power density</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering of Polyanion Type Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Toward Higher Energy/Power Density</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Huangxu; Xu, Ming; Zhang, Zhian; Lai, Yanqing; Ma, Jianmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">28</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000473</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The development of high energy/power d. sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is still challenged by the high redox potential of Na/Na+ and large radius of Na+ ions, thus requiring extensive further improvement to, in particular, enhance the capacity and voltage of cathode materials.  Among the various types of cathodes, the polyanion cathodes have emerged as the most pragmatic option due to their outstanding thermostability, unique inductive effect, and flexible structures.  In this Review, a crit. overview of the design principles and engineering strategies of polyanion cathodes that could have a pivotal role in developing high energy/power d. SIBs are presented.  Specifically, the engineering of polyanion cathode materials for higher voltage and specific capacity to increase energy d. is discussed.  The way in which morphol. control, architectural design, and electrode processing have been developed to increase power d. for SIBs is also analyzed.  Finally, the remaining challenges and the future research direction of this field are presented.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202010041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ran, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Design strategies of 3D carbon-based electrodes for charge/ion transport in lithium ion battery and sodium ion battery</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/adfm.202010041</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D31%26publication_year%3D2021%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D17%26author%3DT.%2BZhang%26author%3DF.%2BRan%26title%3DDesign%2Bstrategies%2Bof%2B3D%2Bcarbon-based%2Belectrodes%2Bfor%2Bcharge%252Fion%2Btransport%2Bin%2Blithium%2Bion%2Bbattery%2Band%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbattery%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.202010041&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.202010041&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Design Strategies of 3D Carbon-Based Electrodes for Charge/Ion Transport in Lithium Ion Battery and Sodium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Tianyun; Ran, Fen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2010041</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Advanced 3D carbon-based electrodes have the potential to significantly enhance the energy-power d. of lithium ion batteries and sodium ion batteries, due to their continuous conductive networks, proper porosity distribution, and integrated stable structure.  However, it still remains a fundamental scientific challenge to accurately understand the charge/ion transport in 3D carbon-based electrodes.  In this , the operating mechanism of charge/ion transport in 3D carbon-based electrodes are comprehended by introducing a useful architectural analogy to provide a phys. insight.  In order to better understand the relationship between 3D carbon-based electrode structure and electrode process characteristics, the main design strategies of 3D carbonbased electrodes according to the specific characteristic of pore tortuosity is proposed.  Through anal. of 3D carbon electrode architectural models, several key scientific issues and related characterization technologies that are beneficial to improving the charge/ion transport efficiency are also raised.  The kinetics difference of ionic transport between Li+ and Na+ ions is also taken into account.  Furthermore, the crit. parameters of porous structure including porosity and tortuosity to investigate the parameter-structure-performance relationships of 3D carbon-based architecture electrodes are highlighted, which in turn would guide more rational battery design in tradeoff between the high capacity and fast transport.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.131951"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of presodiated B, N Co-doped carbon materials and application in sodium ions batteries with enhanced initial coulombic efficiency</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>427</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">131951</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2021.131951</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D427%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DY.%2BTang%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26author%3DD.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BMao%26title%3DSynthesis%2Bof%2Bpresodiated%2BB%252C%2BN%2BCo-doped%2Bcarbon%2Bmaterials%2Band%2Bapplication%2Bin%2Bsodium%2Bions%2Bbatteries%2Bwith%2Benhanced%2Binitial%2Bcoulombic%2Befficiency%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2021.131951&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2021.131951&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of presodiated B, N Co-doped carbon materials and application in sodium ions batteries with enhanced initial coulombic efficiency</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Yihua; Wang, Xinxin; Chen, Jingjing; Wang, Dajian; Mao, Zhiyong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">427</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">131951</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatoms doped carbon-based materials have attracted abundant attention as an anode material in high-energy d. and low-cost sodium ions batteries (SIBs).  However, the low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) resulted from the irreversible Na trapping and the formation of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is denounced in the practical application.  In this work, presodiated B and N co-doped carbons are fabricated by a facial one-step synthetic process employing graphitic carbon nitride (g-C3N4) as precursor and NaBH4 as both presodiation agent and B sources.  The high doping levels of B and N in the resultant carbon materials lead to a promising Na+ storage capability (308 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1) when served as the anode in SIBs.  More importantly, desirable ICE as high as 96.1% was recorded for the obtained presodiated B, N co-doped carbon material benefiting from the pre-incorporated sodium, which passivates the irreversible reactive sites.  This work provides a novel route to realize simultaneous presodiation and B, N co-doping within carbon materials, enabling promising Na+ storage capability and enhanced ICE for application in SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202003854"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Probing the energy storage mechanism of quasi-metallic Na in hard carbon for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">11</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2003854</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202003854</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2021%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26issue%3D11%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BFeng%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26author%3DH.%2BYang%26author%3DR.%2BDong%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BXu%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DH.%2BGao%26title%3DProbing%2Bthe%2Benergy%2Bstorage%2Bmechanism%2Bof%2Bquasi-metallic%2BNa%2Bin%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202003854&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202003854&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Probing the Energy Storage Mechanism of Quasi-Metallic Na in Hard Carbon for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Zhaohua; Feng, Xin; Bai, Ying; Yang, Haoyi; Dong, Ruiqi; Wang, Xinran; Xu, Huajie; Wang, Qiyu; Li, Hong; Gao, Hongcai; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2003854</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon (HC) is the most promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), nevertheless, the understanding of sodium storage mechanism in HC is very limited.  As an important aspect of storage mechanism, the steady state of sodium stored in HC has not been revealed clearly to date.  Herein, the formation mechanism of quasi-metallic sodium and the quasi-ionic bond between sodium and carbon within the electrochem. reaction on the basis of theor. calcns. are disclosed.  The presence of quasi-metallic sodium is further confirmed with the assistance of a specific reaction between the sodiated HC electrode and ethanol, by analyzing the reaction products with Fourier-transform IR spectroscopy, gas chromatog., and NMR.  Moreover, based on the specific chem. reaction, the compn. of fully sodiated HC is estd. to be NaC6.7, and the corresponding capacity of sucrose-derived HC is calcd. to be 333.4 mAh g-1 in SIBs, matching well with the exptl. result.  This work helps to reveal the steady state of sodium and improve the understanding of sodium storage behavior in HC from the aspect of charge transfer.  In addn., the proposed method is also expected to pave the way to investigate sodium storage mechanisms in other electrode systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref7" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1002/sus2.198"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Significantly enhanced ion-migration and sodium-storage capability derived by strongly coupled dual interfacial engineering in heterogeneous bimetallic sulfides with densified carbon matrix</span>. <i>SusMat</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e198</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

High-energy batteries with low cost are urgently needed in the field of large-scale energy storage, such as grid systems and renewable energy sources.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) with alloy-based anodes provide huge potential due to their earth abundance, high capacity, and suitable working potential, and are recognized as attractive alternatives for next-generation batteries system.  Although some important breakthroughs have been reported, more significant improvements are still required for long lifetime and high energy d.  Herein, the latest progress for alloy-based anodes for SIBs and PIBs is summarized, mainly including Sn, Sb, Ge, Bi, Si, P, and their oxides, sulfides, selenides, and phosphides.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anchoring SnS2 on TiC/C Backbone to Promote Sodium Ion Storage by Phosphate Ion Doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Yanbin; Deng, Shengjue; Liu, Ping; Zhang, Yan; Li, Yahao; Tong, Xili; Shen, Hong; Liu, Qi; Pan, Guoxiang; Zhang, Lingjie; Wang, Xiuli; Xia, Xinhui; Tu, Jiangping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin disulfide (SnS2) shows promising properties toward sodium ion storage with high capacity, but its cycle life and high rate capability are still undermined as a result of poor reaction kinetics and unstable structure.  In this work, phosphate ion (PO43-)-doped SnS2 (P-SnS2) nanoflake arrays on conductive TiC/C backbone are reported to form high-quality P-SnS2@TiC/C arrays via a hydrothermal-chem. vapor deposition method.  By virtue of the synergistic effect between PO43- doping and conductive network of TiC/C arrays, enhanced electronic cond. and enlarged interlayer spacing are realized in the designed P-SnS2@TiC/C arrays.  Moreover, the introduced PO43- can result in favorable intercalation/deintercalation of Na+ and accelerate electrochem. reaction kinetics.  Notably, lower bandgap and enhanced electronic cond. owing to the introduction of PO43- are demonstrated by d. function theory calcns. and UV-visible absorption spectra.  In view of these pos. factors above, the P-SnS2@TiC/C electrode delivers a high capacity of 1293.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and exhibits good rate capability (476.7 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), much better than the SnS2@TiC/C counterpart.  This work may trigger new enthusiasm on construction of advanced metal sulfide electrodes for application in rechargeable alkali ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref16" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201907023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A water stable, near-zero-strain O3-layered titanium-based anode for long cycle sodium-ion battery</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal (TM) oxides NaxMO2 (M = TM) showed great promise in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs); however, they are extremely sensitive to moisture.  To date, most reported titanium-based layered anodes exhibit a P2-type structure.  But O3-type compds. are rarely studied and their synthesis is challenging due to their higher percentage of unstable Ti3+ than the P2 type.  Here, a pure phase and highly cryst. O3-type Na0.73Li0.36Ti0.73O2 with high performance is successfully proposed in SIBs.  This material delivers a reversible capacity of 108 mAh/g with a stable and safe potential of 0.75 V vs. Na/Na+.  In situ x-ray diffraction reveals that this material does not undergo any phase transitions and exhibits a near-zero vol. change upon Na+ insertion/de-insertion, which ensures exceptional long cycle life over 6000 cycles.  Importantly, this O3-Na0.73Li0.36Ti0.73O2 shows superior moisture stability, even when immersed into water, which are both elusive for conventional layered TM oxides in SIBs.  It is believed that the small interlayer distance and high occupation of interlayer vacancy promise such unprecedented water stability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2022.139768"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Insights on Titanium-based chalcogenides TiX2 (X= O, S, Se) as LIBs/SIBs anode materials</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights on Titanium-based chalcogenides TiX2 (X = O, S, Se) as LIBs/SIBs anode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chai, Jiali; Han, Ning; Feng, Shihui; Huang, Xiaoxiong; Tang, Bohejin; Zhang, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Ti-based chalcogenides TiX2 (X = O, S, Se) are widely used in the research of battery electrode materials due to its excellent rate performance and good chem. stability.  In this paper, in order to improve the electrochem. performance of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium ion batteries (SIBs), and further improve the application prospect of batteries, the strategies for design and prepn. of LIBs/SIBs anode materials for Ti-based chalcogenides TiX2 (X = O, S, Se) are reviewed. On this basis, the application prospect of TiX2 (X = O, S, Se) as LIBs/SIBs anode is prospected, it is expected to fill the research of diversified applications of LIBs/SIBs anode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1007/s10853-020-05733-w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Intergranular passivation of the TiC coating for enhancing corrosion resistance and surface conductivity in stainless-steel bipolar plates</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intergranular passivation of the TiC coating for enhancing corrosion resistance and surface conductivity in stainless-steel bipolar plates</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jingling; Xu, Zeling; Li, Yujian; Ma, Xinzhou; Mo, Jiamei; Weng, Lingyan; Liu, Cuiyin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">56</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8689-8703</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Abstr.: Stainless-steel bipolar plates (BPPs) are of great significance in low-cost, easily processable, lightwt. proton exchange membrane fuel cells (PEMFCs) despite the challenge presented by corrosion in protective coatings.  Localized corrosion along the grain boundaries in a crystal film is common, but few preventive measures were developed so far.  Thus, the authors propose a novel strategy using a Ta and C co-modification to improve the chem. stability of Ti carbide (TiC)-based coatings (Cr/Ta/TiC/C).  During the film growth, the subjacent Ta atoms were thermally diffused throughout the columnar structure of TiC and reacted with the C layer.  The reaction product, i.e., TaC, acted as a chem. passivator to the grain boundary.  Combined with the C capping layer, these functional layers synergistically suppressed any localized corrosion.  Therefore, corrosion current densities within the United States Department of Energy's tech. recommendations were achieved in both potentiostatic and potentiodynamic polarization.  Meanwhile, by controlling the Ta metal dispersion, the interfacial contact resistance between the multilayer structure and the C paper can be reduced to 7.1 mΩ cm-2 at a compaction force of 140 N cm-2.  The substantial improvement in the corrosion resistance and cond. of BPP places the authors' work among the most efficient anticorrosion systems in PEMFC applications reported so far.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref19" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1111/jace.16810"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yun, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile synthesis of high-melting point spherical TiC and TiN powders at low temperature</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure, optical properties and thermal stability of TiC-based tandem spectrally selective solar absorber coating</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gao, Xiang-Hu; Guo, Zhi-Ming; Geng, Qing-Fen; Ma, Peng-Jun; Liu, Gang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Solar Energy Materials &amp; Solar Cells</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">157</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">543-549</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SEMCEQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0927-0248</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new spectrally selective solar absorber coating of TiC/Al2O3 is prepd. on stainless steel substrate using a magnetron sputtering method.  The new coating exhibits a high absorptance of 0.92 and a low emittance of 0.13 (82 °C).  The tandem absorber is characterized using ultra-high resoln. scanning electron microscope, UV-vis-NIR spectrophotometer, Fourier transform IR spectroscopy (FTIR), X-ray diffraction (XRD), XPS and Raman spectroscopy.  The formation of amorphous carbon is due to the dissocn. of TiC layer deposited under high substrate temp. (300 °C).  The diffused carbon at 600-800 °C with mixed sp2 and sp3 bonds is further demonstrated by XPS and Raman spectra.  With an increase in annealing temp., the surface structure becomes more graphitic.  The tandem absorber is stable in vacuum up to 650 °C for 2 h, indicating its importance for high temp. solar selective applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref21" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.ijrmhm.2022.105879"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of TiC content on the microstructure and mechanical properties of Ti-30Mo-xTiC composites</span>. <i>International Journal of Refractory Metals and Hard Materials</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>107</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">105879</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kovar, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Laser chemical vapor deposition of TiC on tantalum</span>. <i>J. Mater. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2002</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>37</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">689</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">697</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1023/A:1013871326880</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D37%26publication_year%3D2002%26pages%3D689-697%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BSci.%26author%3DM.%2BS.%2BNoel%26author%3DD.%2BKovar%26title%3DLaser%2Bchemical%2Bvapor%2Bdeposition%2Bof%2BTiC%2Bon%2Btantalum%26doi%3D10.1023%252FA%253A1013871326880&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;doiOfLink=10.1023%2FA%3A1013871326880&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Laser chemical vapor deposition of TiC on tantalum</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Noel, M. Shane; Kovar, D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2002</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">37</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">689-697</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMTSAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0022-2461</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Kluwer Academic Publishers</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Laser chem. vapor deposition (LCVD) of TiC coatings on Ta substrates using H gas, Ti tetrachloride (TiCl4) and either methane (CH4) or acetylene (C2H2) source gases was investigated.  The influences of the molar ratio of the source gases and the deposition temp. on the phase assemblage, compn., and morphol. of the coatings was examd.  Using C2H2, nearly stoichiometric coatings were produced at 1000°C and at a TiCl4/C2H2 ratio of 1/0.4.  Stoichiometric coatings were also produced using CH4 but the deposition temp. was 400° higher and a much larger fraction of the carbon source was required compared to C2H2.  Although deposition rates were much slower when using CH4, the coatings exhibited a smoother surface finish and had a higher d. compared to those produced using C2H2.  The suitability of CH4 and C2H2 as C sources for depositing stoichiometric, phase-pure coatings is discussed in light of these results.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1021/ja00239a053"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Girolami, G. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jensen, J. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pollina, D. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Allocca, C. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kaloyeros, A. E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Williams, W. S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Organometallic route to the chemical vapor deposition of titanium carbide films at exceptionally low temperatures</span>. <i>J. Am.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct synthesis and chemical vapor deposition of 2D carbide and nitride MXenes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Di; Zhou, Chenkun; Filatov, Alexander S.; Cho, Wooje; Lagunas, Francisco; Wang, Mingzhan; Vaikuntanathan, Suriyanarayanan; Liu, Chong; Klie, Robert F.; Talapin, Dmitri V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">379</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6638</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1242-1247</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SCIEAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1095-9203</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional transition-metal carbides and nitrides (MXenes) are a large family of materials actively studied for various applications, esp. in the field of energy storage.  MXenes are commonly synthesized by etching the layered ternary compds., called MAX phases.  We demonstrate a direct synthetic route for scalable and atom-economic synthesis of MXenes, including compds. that have not been synthesized from MAX phases, by the reactions of metals and metal halides with graphite, methane, or nitrogen.  The direct synthesis enables chem. vapor deposition growth of MXene carpets and complex spherulite-like morphologies that form through buckling and release of MXene carpet to expose fresh surface for further reaction.  The directly synthesized MXenes showed excellent energy storage capacity for lithium-ion intercalation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpcc.8b03425"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Two-dimensional tetragonal titanium carbide: A high-capacity and high-rate battery material</span>. <i>J. Phys. Chem. C</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>122</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">27</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">15118</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">15124</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional Tetragonal Titanium Carbide: a High-Capacity and High-Rate Battery Material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Dong; Lu, Shaohua; Guo, Yundong; Hu, Xiaojun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">122</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15118-15124</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-performance electrode materials are crit. for the development of next-generation energy conversion and storage systems.  Herein, we report a theor. design of novel two-dimensional materials, namely, tetragonal titanium carbide and nitride (tetr-TiC and tetr-TiN) based on ab initio calcns.  State-of-the-art calcns. show that tetr-TiC and tetr-TiN deliver the intrinsic metallic nature, high thermal stability, and satisfactory lithium-ion storage and rate capability.  More importantly, compared with previously known Ti3C2 and Ti2C sheets, the proposed new material has lower Li diffusion barrier, higher theor. capacity, and lower av. open circuit.  Combining such advanced features, the proposed tetragonal TiC is a promising candidate for future lithium-ion batteries, supercapacitors, and fuel cells.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1021/acsanm.2c02781"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.07.081</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D269%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D848-854%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DI.%2BT.%2BKim%26author%3DS.-O.%2BKim%26author%3DA.%2BManthiram%26title%3DEffect%2Bof%2BTiC%2Baddition%2Bon%2BSnSb%25E2%2580%2593C%2Bcomposite%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2014.07.081&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2014.07.081&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of TiC addition on SnSb-C composite anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Il Tae; Kim, Sang-Ok; Manthiram, Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">269</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">848-854</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin-antimony alloy (SnSb) particles dispersed in a conductive matrix comprized of TiC and carbon have been synthesized by high energy mech. milling (HEMM) and explored as anodes for sodium-ion batteries.  The SnSb-TiC-C samples have been prepd. with different TiC and carbon contents in the composite, characterized by x-ray diffraction before and after sodiation and by high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, and compared to SnSb-C as a baseline.  The SnSb-TiC-C anodes demonstrate better cyclic performance as well as better rate-capability compared to SnSb-C.  In addn., the increase in TiC content in the composite leads to better electrochem. performance.  SnSb-TiC(40%)-C(20%) and SnSb-TiC(40%)-C(30%) electrodes exhibit the best electrochem. performance, which could result from both the well-developed SnSb as an electrochem. active nanocryst. material and the conductive matrix composed of a combination of TiC and carbon.  Addnl., the use of FEC electrolyte additive results in much better electrochem. performance even at high-rate c.d. when combined with this material due to the formation of a stable and thin SEI layer.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref55" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1039/c4cp01240b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, I. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Allcorn, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manthiram, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-performance FeSb–TiC–C nanocomposite anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Phys. Chem. Chem. Phys.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">25</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">12884</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">12889</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c4cp01240b</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D16%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D12884-12889%26journal%3DPhys.%2BChem.%2BChem.%2BPhys.%26issue%3D25%26author%3DI.%2BT.%2BKim%26author%3DE.%2BAllcorn%26author%3DA.%2BManthiram%26title%3DHigh-performance%2BFeSb%25E2%2580%2593TiC%25E2%2580%2593C%2Bnanocomposite%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc4cp01240b&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc4cp01240b&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref56" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.01.163"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, I. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Allcorn, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manthiram, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cu6Sn5–TiC–C nanocomposite anodes for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>281</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">11</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">17</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.01.163</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D281%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D11-17%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DI.%2BT.%2BKim%26author%3DE.%2BAllcorn%26author%3DA.%2BManthiram%26title%3DCu6Sn5%25E2%2580%2593TiC%25E2%2580%2593C%2Bnanocomposite%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Bhigh-performance%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2015.01.163&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2015.01.163&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cu6Sn5-TiC-C nanocomposite anodes for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Il Tae; Allcorn, Eric; Manthiram, Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">281</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11-17</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cu6Sn5 alloy nanoparticles dispersed in a TiC and C conductive matrix have been developed via high energy mech. milling, and the resulting Cu6Sn5-TiC-C nanocomposite has been evaluated as anodes for sodium-ion batteries.  Composite anodes of Sn-C exhibit poor cyclic performance even with the introduction of 2 vol.% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) additive into the electrolyte.  In contrast, Cu6Sn5-TiC-C nanocomposite anodes exhibit stable cycle life corresponding to a capacity retention of ∼80% at 40 cycles and high-rate performance with a capacity retention of ∼62% at 3000 mA/g.  These superior performance metrics is ascribed to the well-developed electrochem. active nanocryst. material (Cu6Sn5) as well as a hybrid conductive matrix (TiC and C).  The incorporation of 2 vol.% FEC additive into the electrolyte further improves the performance of Cu6Sn5-TiC-C nanocomposite to display a capacity retention of ∼94% at 250 cycles and high-rate capacity retention of ∼82% at 5000 mA/g, which are attributed to the formation of a thin and stable solid electrolyte interface layer in presence of FEC.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref57" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1016/j.apsusc.2023.158564"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sufyan, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abbas, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sajjad, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Larsson, J. A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Monolayer TiC─A high-performance Dirac anode with ultralow diffusion barriers and high energy densities for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>Appl. Surf. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>642</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">158564</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.apsusc.2023.158564</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D642%26publication_year%3D2024%26journal%3DAppl.%2BSurf.%2BSci.%26author%3DA.%2BSufyan%26author%3DG.%2BAbbas%26author%3DM.%2BSajjad%26author%3DJ.%2BA.%2BLarsson%26title%3DMonolayer%2BTiC%25E2%2594%2580A%2Bhigh-performance%2BDirac%2Banode%2Bwith%2Bultralow%2Bdiffusion%2Bbarriers%2Band%2Bhigh%2Benergy%2Bdensities%2Bfor%2BLi-ion%2Band%2BNa-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.apsusc.2023.158564&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.apsusc.2023.158564&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R

                10.1038/s41598-023-42954-w</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DSci.%2BRep.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DF.%2BShirvani%26author%3DM.%2BR.%2BJafari%26author%3DA.%2BShokri%26title%3DEffect%2Bof%2Balloying%2BLi%2Bon%2Blithium-ion%2Bbatteries%2Bapplicability%2Bof%2Btwo-dimensional%2BTiN%2Band%2BTiC%2Bas%2Bnovel%2Belectrode%2Bmaterials%253A%2Ba%2Bfirst%2Bprinciple%2Bstudy%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fs41598-023-42954-w&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03597&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fs41598-023-42954-w&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">51</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">61116</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">61128</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.1c18234</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Design of Unique MoSe2-Carbon Nanobowl Particles Endows Superior Alkali Metal-Ion Storage Beyond Lithium</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Lai; Li, Jie; Wang, Gongrui; Peng, Bo; Liu, Rong; Shi, Liang; Zhang, Genqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">61116-61128</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Attracted by the rich earth abundance and low-cost advantages, alkali metal-ion (Na/K)-based energy storage devices have attracted wide interest as promising candidates for energy economizing in recent years.  Unfortunately, the lack of suitable host materials with high capacity and long life span for alkali metal-ion storage has severely impeded their practical application in large-scale energy storage devices.  Herein, we present a promising anode candidate composed of ultrasmall MoSe2 clusters embedded in a nitrogen-doped hollow carbon nanobowl substrate to form unique MoSe2-Carbon nanobowl particles (denoted as MoSe2(CNB)).  MoSe2(CNB) demonstrates exceptional electrochem. properties for alkali metal-ion storage including sodium and potassium.  In situ Raman spectroscopy and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. measurements reveal the possible reason for the high performance of MoSe2(CNB).  Notably, the assembled potassium-ion hybrid capacitors could manifest an extraordinary energy d. of 130.7 W h kg-1 at 0.2 A g-1, a high power d. of 13,607 W kg-1, and an enviable cycle life after 6000 cycles, further reflecting the great developmental potential for energy storage devices in practical applications.  This work provides a new method to design functional nanostructures for electrode materials to drive the development and application of possible energy storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202000473"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineering of polyanion type cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries: toward higher energy/power density</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>30</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">28</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2000473</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202000473</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering of Polyanion Type Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Toward Higher Energy/Power Density</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Huangxu; Xu, Ming; Zhang, Zhian; Lai, Yanqing; Ma, Jianmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">28</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000473</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The development of high energy/power d. sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is still challenged by the high redox potential of Na/Na+ and large radius of Na+ ions, thus requiring extensive further improvement to, in particular, enhance the capacity and voltage of cathode materials.  Among the various types of cathodes, the polyanion cathodes have emerged as the most pragmatic option due to their outstanding thermostability, unique inductive effect, and flexible structures.  In this Review, a crit. overview of the design principles and engineering strategies of polyanion cathodes that could have a pivotal role in developing high energy/power d. SIBs are presented.  Specifically, the engineering of polyanion cathode materials for higher voltage and specific capacity to increase energy d. is discussed.  The way in which morphol. control, architectural design, and electrode processing have been developed to increase power d. for SIBs is also analyzed.  Finally, the remaining challenges and the future research direction of this field are presented.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202010041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ran, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Design strategies of 3D carbon-based electrodes for charge/ion transport in lithium ion battery and sodium ion battery</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>31</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">17</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2010041</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202010041</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Design Strategies of 3D Carbon-Based Electrodes for Charge/Ion Transport in Lithium Ion Battery and Sodium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Tianyun; Ran, Fen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2010041</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Advanced 3D carbon-based electrodes have the potential to significantly enhance the energy-power d. of lithium ion batteries and sodium ion batteries, due to their continuous conductive networks, proper porosity distribution, and integrated stable structure.  However, it still remains a fundamental scientific challenge to accurately understand the charge/ion transport in 3D carbon-based electrodes.  In this , the operating mechanism of charge/ion transport in 3D carbon-based electrodes are comprehended by introducing a useful architectural analogy to provide a phys. insight.  In order to better understand the relationship between 3D carbon-based electrode structure and electrode process characteristics, the main design strategies of 3D carbonbased electrodes according to the specific characteristic of pore tortuosity is proposed.  Through anal. of 3D carbon electrode architectural models, several key scientific issues and related characterization technologies that are beneficial to improving the charge/ion transport efficiency are also raised.  The kinetics difference of ionic transport between Li+ and Na+ ions is also taken into account.  Furthermore, the crit. parameters of porous structure including porosity and tortuosity to investigate the parameter-structure-performance relationships of 3D carbon-based architecture electrodes are highlighted, which in turn would guide more rational battery design in tradeoff between the high capacity and fast transport.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.131951"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of presodiated B, N Co-doped carbon materials and application in sodium ions batteries with enhanced initial coulombic efficiency</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>427</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">131951</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2021.131951</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatoms doped carbon-based materials have attracted abundant attention as an anode material in high-energy d. and low-cost sodium ions batteries (SIBs).  However, the low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) resulted from the irreversible Na trapping and the formation of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is denounced in the practical application.  In this work, presodiated B and N co-doped carbons are fabricated by a facial one-step synthetic process employing graphitic carbon nitride (g-C3N4) as precursor and NaBH4 as both presodiation agent and B sources.  The high doping levels of B and N in the resultant carbon materials lead to a promising Na+ storage capability (308 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1) when served as the anode in SIBs.  More importantly, desirable ICE as high as 96.1% was recorded for the obtained presodiated B, N co-doped carbon material benefiting from the pre-incorporated sodium, which passivates the irreversible reactive sites.  This work provides a novel route to realize simultaneous presodiation and B, N co-doping within carbon materials, enabling promising Na+ storage capability and enhanced ICE for application in SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202003854"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Probing the energy storage mechanism of quasi-metallic Na in hard carbon for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Adv.
